I. INTRODUCTION

A. Description of Project
The River Arts District Transportation Improvement Project (RADTIP) is proposed to be
located along the French Broad River on both new and existing location following Lyman
Street and Riverside Drive in Asheville, NC. The purpose of the project is to improve the
existing roadway geometric deficiencies and to enhance multimodal mobility and system
linkages. As part of the development of alternatives for the different alignments of the
RADTIP, a capacity analysis for the 2010 Existing, 2035 No-Build, and 2035 Build
Alternatives was performed. This capacity analysis will determine the existing and
potential future capacity deficiencies and help develop mitigation measures for enhanced
traffic operations.

B. Existing Conditions
Lyman Street is a two-lane undivided, 24-foot wide, local collector roadway section.
Lyman Street runs along the French Broad River from Amboy Road at the southern project
terminus to Riverside Drive at the northern terminus. The posted speed limit on Lyman
Street is 30 miles per hour (MPH). The land uses in this area are primarily industrial.




                                        Lyman Street looking East


Riverside Drive is a two-lane undivided, 24-foot wide, local collector roadway section.
Riverside Drive runs along the French Broad River from Lyman Street to the south until
becoming Old Marshall Highway (NC 251) to the north. The posted speed limit on
Riverside Drive is 30 MPH. The land uses in this area are primarily industrial and
commercial.




March 26, 2012                                                                    Page 2
River Arts District Transportation Improvement Project
Capacity Analysis Report




                                      Riverside Drive looking South


Craven Street is a two-lane undivided, 24-foot wide, local collector roadway section. It
provides a local connection to portions of the city west of the French Broad River. West of
the intersection with Riverside Drive, Craven Street is known as West Haywood Street.
There is no posted speed limit on Craven Street/West Haywood Street. The land uses in
this area are primarily commercial and open space.




                                     Haywood Street looking West


Amboy Road is a two-lane undivided, 24-foot wide, local collector roadway section. It
provides a local connection to portions of the city west of the French Broad River, running
east to west from Lyman Street to I-240/I-26. The posted speed limit on Amboy Road is
45 MPH. The land uses in this area are primarily park and open space areas.

II. TRAFFIC COUNTS

Existing traffic counts were completed by CDM Smith from June 7th ­ 11th, 2010 at the
following intersections:

    ·    Hill Street / Riverside Drive
    ·    US 19/23 On-Ramp / Riverside Drive
    ·    Craven Street / Riverside Drive
    ·    Lyman Street / Riverside Drive
    ·    Lyman Street / Amboy Road

Raw count data for these locations are included in Appendix A. Traffic volumes at these
intersections during the AM and PM peak hours are shown on Figure 3.

III. TRAFFIC FORECASTS DEVELOPMENT METHODOLOGY

To develop 2035 No-Build traffic volumes, CDM Smith adjusted outputs from the French
Broad River 2035 Travel Demand Model (TDM), as discussed below. The proposed I-26
Connector was included in the TDM but was eliminated to develop the 2035 No-Build
forecasts for the RADTIP Project as the timeline to implement the Connector has not been
identified. The I-26 Connector would link the I-26/I-40/I-240 interchange southwest of
the city to the US 19/US 23/US 70 north of the city.

As discussed in Appendix B, forecasts were developed for the 2035 No-Build and Build
scenarios. By removing the I-26 Connector, trips that would otherwise by-pass the RADTIP
are compelled to travel along it. Figure 4 shows the adjusted TDM outputs for key links in
the system and the peak hour turning movement volumes upon which the 2035 No-Build
and Build scenarios are built.

IV. TRAFFIC CAPACITY ANALYSIS

A. Methodology
The five study area intersections were analyzed using the methods outlined in the Highway
Capacity Manual1 and Synchro Version 7.0 Software. The Highway Capacity Manual
defines capacity as "the maximum rate of flow at which persons or vehicles can be
reasonably expected to traverse a point or uniform section of a lane or roadway during
a specified time period under prevailing roadway, traffic, and control conditions, usually
expressed as vehicles per hour or persons per hour".

Level of service (LOS) is a term used to represent different traffic conditions, and is
defined as a "qualitative measure describing operational conditions within a traffic
stream, and their perception by motorist or passengers". Level of Service varies from
Level A, representing free flow, to Level F, where traffic breakdown conditions are
evident. Level B represents good progression with minimal congestion. At Level C, the
number of vehicles stopping is noticeable, although many still pass through the intersection
without stopping. Level D represents more congestion, but the overall operations are
acceptable. At Level E, freedom to maneuver within the traffic stream is extremely
difficult with driver frustration being generally high.

For signalized intersections, service levels pertain to each approach as well as an overall
value. The unsignalized intersection analysis method in the Highway Capacity Manual
assigns LOS values for each movement that yields the right-of-way, but not to the overall
intersection. This movement is generally a secondary movement from a minor street. At an
unsignalized intersection, the primary traffic on the main roadway is virtually
uninterrupted. Therefore, the overall LOS is usually much greater than what is
represented by the results of the minor street movements. Synchro Version 7.0 will
calculate an average amount of delay for the overall intersection, but will not assign a
LOS value. Therefore, the overall intersection delay as well as the amount of delay on the
minor street is reported in the summary tables of this report. Generally, LOS D is
acceptable for signalized intersections in suburban areas during peak periods. With the
current method of reporting LOS for unsignalized intersections, it is not uncommon for some
of the minor street movements to be operating at a LOS F during the peak hours. Table 1
presents criteria of each LOS as indicated in the Highway Capacity Manual.

Synchro 7.0 calculated the level of service and delay for each intersection using methods
outlined in the Highway Capacity Manual. All capacity analyses are included in Appendix
C and are briefly summarized in the following sub-sections.




March 26, 2012                                                                      Page 10
River Arts District Transportation Improvement Project

                                                LEVEL OF SERVICE CRITERIA

            SIGNALIZED INTERSECTIONS                                             UNSIGNALIZED INTERSECTIONS

          Level of                 Stopped Delay                                 Level of              Average Total Delay
          Service                 Per Vehicle (sec)                              Service                    (sec/veh)

               A                          <10.0                                       A                            <10

               B                 >10.0 and <20.0                                      B                     >10 and <15

               C                 >20.0 and <35.0                                      C                     >15 and <25

               D                 >35.0 and <55.0                                      D                     >25 and <35

               E                 >55.0 and <80.0                                       E                    >35 and <50

               F                          >80.0                                       F                            >50

    Source: Highway Capacity Manual

B. No-Build Traffic Capacity Analysis Results
For the 2010 Existing condition, all five study intersections operate at an overall
acceptable level of service (LOS C or better). During the 2035 No-Build conditions,
operations degrade due to the increased traffic using the study area roadways. The
increase in traffic volumes would be largely handled by the proposed I-26 Connector,
although this link was not included for this analysis. Table 2 is a summary of the LOS at
the study area intersections for both the 2010 Existing and 2035 No-Build conditions.

Hill Street / Riverside Drive
The unsignalized intersection of Hill Street / Riverside Drive is currently operating with
very low overall and minor movement delays. The minor westbound movement currently
operates at LOS B during the AM peak hour and LOS C during the PM peak hour. The
westbound movement from Hill Street deteriorates to LOS F during the AM peak and LOS
D during the PM peak for the 2035 No-Build scenario. Analysis of the Build alternatives
explored measures which could be undertaken to improve conditions at this intersection, as
discussed in the following section.

US 19/23 On-Ramp / Riverside Drive
The unsignalized intersection at the US 19/23 On-Ramp and Riverside Drive is currently
operating with very low overall and minor movement delays and is expected to continue
to operate at an acceptable level in 2035. The southbound left turning movement
currently operates at LOS A during the AM and PM peak hours. The southbound left
turning movement is expected to operate at LOS B during the AM and PM peak hours in
the 2035 No-Build scenario.

Craven Street / Riverside Drive
The signalized intersection of Craven Street / Riverside Drive is currently operating at
LOS B in the AM peak hour and LOS C in the PM peak hour. During the 2035 No-Build
scenario, this intersection is expected to operate at LOS C during the AM peak hour and
LOS E during the PM peak hour. Analysis of the Build alternatives explored measures
which could be undertaken to improve conditions at this intersection, as discussed in the
following section.

Lyman Street / Riverside Drive
The unsignalized intersection of Lyman Street / Riverside Drive is currently operating with
very low overall and minor movement delays. The southbound movements from Riverside
Drive currently operate at LOS B during the AM and PM peak hours. In 2035, operations
at this intersection fail if no improvements are made. Analysis of the Build alternatives
explored measures which could be undertaken to improve conditions at this intersection, as
discussed in the following section.

Lyman Street / Amboy Road
The signalized intersection of Lyman Street / Amboy Road is currently operating at LOS B
in the AM peak hour and LOS A in the PM peak hour. During the 2035 No-Build scenario,
this intersection is expected to operate at LOS D in the AM peak hour and LOS B in the
PM peak hour. Analysis of the Build alternatives explored measures which could be
undertaken to improve conditions at this intersection, as discussed in the following section.

C. Build Traffic Capacity Analysis Results
Several alternatives were developed for the RADTIP transportation improvement project,
as shown in Figure 5. With the exception of the Lyman Street / Riverside Drive
intersection, the study area intersections remain at their existing location for each
alternative. Construction of the project is not anticipated to induce any additional trips
when compared to the No-Build volumes. The build capacity analysis examined potential
small-scale intersection improvements that could be incorporated into the project to
improve operations at the five study area intersections.

Hill Street / Riverside Drive
In the 2035 No-Build scenario, the unsignalized Hill Street / Riverside Drive intersection
would experience an average delay of 16.5 seconds/vehicle during the AM peak hour
and 6.1 seconds/vehicle during the PM peak hour. The westbound left turn movement
would operate at LOS F during the AM peak hour and LOS D during the PM peak hour.
Two improvements were evaluated as part of the Build scenario, which would improve the
intersection at its existing location:
     · Addition of a southbound left turn lane along Riverside Drive with storage space
         for 2-3 cars improves performance during the AM peak hour, reducing delay for
         this movement to LOS E. Operations during the PM peak hour do not change
         noticeably due to the low volume of vehicles making this movement.
     · Extension of the westbound right turn bay from its existing 60-foot length to 100
         feet in length also improves operations.

Table 3 presents a comparison of the 2010 Existing, 2035 No-Build, and 2035 Build
scenarios at this intersection.

US 19/23 On-Ramp / Riverside Drive
In the 2035 No-Build scenario, the unsignalized US 19/23 On-Ramp intersection with
Riverside Drive would operate with minor delay; the southbound left turn movement would
operate at LOS B during both peak hours. No improvements were evaluated as part of
the Build scenario for this intersection.

Craven Street / Riverside Drive
In the 2035 No-Build scenario, the signalized Craven Street / Riverside Drive intersection
would operate at LOS C during the AM peak hour and LOS E during the PM peak hour.
Three improvements were evaluated as part of the Build scenario, which would improve
the intersection at its existing location:
     · Optimization signal timings.

    · Addition of a 50-foot long turn bay along Craven Street for southbound left turn

Lyman Street / Riverside Drive
In the 2035 No-Build scenario, operations at the unsignalized Lyman Street / Riverside
Drive intersection would fail during the AM peak hour and experience substantial delay
during the PM peak hour. A variety of improvement options were evaluated as part of
the Build scenario, described below. As shown in Figure 5, the Yellow Alternative would
improve along the existing alignment. The Green Alternative would shift the Lyman Street
/ Riverside Drive intersection to the west to address the substandard curve along Lyman
Drive near the stone yard and 12 Bones. Figure 6 presents conceptual sketches of each of
these improvement scenarios.
    · Yellow-1: In this scenario, the intersection would remain at its existing location to
        operate as a three-way stop-controlled intersection.
    · Yellow-2: In this scenario, the intersection would be reconstructed as a roundabout
        at or near the existing location of the intersection.
    · Green-1: In this scenario, a new T-intersection would be created, shifted west of its
        existing location. Westbound Lyman Street would be stop-controlled; northbound
        Lyman Street and southbound Riverside Drive would not stop.
    · Green-2: In this scenario, a new T-intersection would be created, shifted west of its
        existing location. All three approaches would be stop-controlled.
    · Green-3: In this scenario, a new roundabout would be created, shifted west of
        existing location of the intersection.

Table 5 presents a comparison of the 2010 Existing, 2035 No-Build, and each of the five
2035 Build scenarios at this intersection. As shown, the intersection performs best as a
roundabout at either location. A three-way stop-controlled intersection performs better
than a one-way stop-controlled intersection at either location, but not as well as a
roundabout.

Lyman Street / Amboy Road
In the 2035 No-Build scenario, the signalized Lyman Street / Amboy Road intersection
would operate at LOS D during the AM peak hour and LOS B during the PM peak hour.
Construction of a roundabout at the existing location was evaluated as the Build scenario
for this intersection. However, the intersection operates better as a standard four-leg,
signalized intersection. Table 6 presents a comparison of the 2010 Existing, 2035 No-
Build, and 2035 Build scenario at this intersection.

V. CONCLUSIONS

Based on the capacity analysis performed for the Existing and 2035 No-Build
alternatives, delay will increase substantially as traffic volumes increase if the I-26
Connector project is not built. Construction of the RADTIP project is not anticipated to
induce any additional trips when compared to the No-Build volume. Analysis identified
several minor improvements at study area intersections that could improve operations:
addition of turn bays at Hill Street and Craven Street and construction of a roundabout at
the Lyman Street / Riverside Drive intersection.

Appendix B




             Traffic Forecasting
                Methodology
Traffic Forecast Methodology




Background
The French Broad River Metropolitan Planning Organization (MPO) maintains the French Broad
River 2035 Model. This travel demand model makes use of the TransCAD modeling software,
but is a manual operation model. This means that no portion of the model is automated. The
user is required to manually execute each step of the model using the TransCAD modeling
software. The user's guide document provided with the model lists the model steps and
equations that the user is expected to input while executing the model.

CDM Smith acquired the French Broad River Model from the North Carolina Department of
Transportation (NCDOT) ­ Transportation Planning Branch (TPB). Along with the user's guide
document, CDM Smith acquired the model data sets containing the highway network and
socioeconomic database used in the model. Furthermore, NCDOT provided archived data
outputs from previously executed model runs for the base and future years. The French Broad
River Model base year is 2005. The current planning horizon of the model is 2035.


Initial Forecasts
Initial forecasts were taken from the archived model outputs provided by NCDOT. Efforts were
focused on providing traffic forecasts along the proposed Wilma-Dykeman Riverway corridor. Of
particular importance were sections of present day Amboy Road, Lyman Street, and Riverside
Drive. A review of the base year model outputs revealed a fairly consistent under-assignment of
volumes along Lyman Street and Riverside Drive from Amboy Road to Hill Street north of I-240.
A set of volume-over-count ratios were developed in order to assess the volume deviation at the
traffic count stations along this corridor. After assessing the deviation in the volumes a set of
adjustment factors were developed that could be applied to forecast volume outputs from the
model. These adjustment factors would help to compensate for the volume deviation
experienced by the base year model and result in more reasonable traffic forecasts. Table 1
identifies the count locations analyzed and the model volumes as compared to the traffic counts.
The adjustment factors are also shown.

 Table 1 - 2005 Base Year Model Results
   Count                                                 Traffic Model    Volume / Adjustment
  Station   Street             Location                  Count Volume      Count     Factor
 1000112    Amboy Road         @ Meadow Road             14,000 15,587        1.11        0.90
 1000062    Lyman Street       North of Meadow Road       7,000   3,691       0.53        1.90
 0100772    Riverside Drive    North of Haywood Street    6,900   5,621       0.81        1.23
 1000050    Riverside Drive    North of I-240             6,700   5,621       0.84        1.19
 1000064    Riverside Drive    North of Hill Street       8,800   8,871       1.01        0.99


The archived results for the 2035 Long-Range Transportation Plan Model adjusted using the
adjustment factors derived from the base year model data. The factors were applied to the 2035
Traffic Forecast Methodology


model volume outputs to develop adjusted volumes. These adjusted volumes are listed below in
Table 2.

 Table 2 - 2035 LRTP Model Results
   Count                                                                Model      Adjusted
  Station   Street                        Location                      Volume     Volume
 1000112    Amboy Road                    @ Meadow Road                  15,373      13,808
 1000062    Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Meadow Road             2,315      4,390
 0100772    Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Haywood Street          3,575      4,388
 1000050    Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of I-240                   3,575      4,261
 1000064    Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Hill Street             8,703      8,633


A comparison between the traffic counts in Table 1 and the adjusted volumes in Table 2 shows
that there is little change between traffic volumes from 2005 to 2035 in the study corridor. What
change occurs tends to be in the negative direction. The cause for this appears to be the
presence of a freeway connector between I-240 at Patton Avenue and I-26 south of Pearson
Bridge Road that has been coded into the highway network.


Alternative Forecasts
An alternative forecast was developed that would forecast traffic along the Wilma-Dykeman
Riverway should the I-26 connector not be built. The 2035 Long Range Transportation Plan
model highway network was modified to remove the I-26 connector and all impacted
interchanges and surface street connections were restored to configurations consistent with the
base year highway network. The model was then executed.

The user's guide documentation for the French Broad River model indicated that it was
necessary to run the model's trip distribution process in conjunction with the model's highway
assignment process in an iterative fashion. This was due to the model's use of congested travel
times to calculate trip destinations. After attempting to reach closure with the model after seven
iterations using the manual approach detailed in the user's guide, CDM Smith staff developed a
script in GISDK to automate the process. The model ran for 17 iterations before reaching
closure. The resulting model volumes are shown below in Table 3.

 Table 3 - 2035 LRTP without I-26 Connector Model Results
   Count                                                                Model      Adjusted
  Station    Street                        Location                     Volume     Volume
 1000112     Amboy Road                    @ Meadow Road                 16,966      15,239
 1000062     Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Meadow Road            6,227     11,808
 0100772     Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Haywood Street         9,679     11,881
 1000050     Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of I-240                  9,679     11,537
 1000064     Wilma Dykeman Riverway        North of Hill Street          13,559      13,450
Traffic Forecast Methodology


As can be seen by comparing the traffic counts in Table 1 with the adjusted volumes in Table 3,
the general trend along the Wilma-Dykeman Riverway is a significant growth in trips. By
removing the I-26 connector, trips that would otherwise by-pass the Wilma-Dykeman Riverway
are compelled to travel along it. The percent change in traffic from 2005 to 2035 is shown in
Table 4.

 Table 4 - Percent Change in Traffic from 2005 to 2035 for Alternative Forecast
   Count                                                                   2005 - 2035
  Station    Street                          Location                         %
 1000112     Amboy Road                      @ Meadow Road                      8.85%
 1000062     Wilma Dykeman Riverway          North of Meadow Road              68.69%
 0100772     Wilma Dykeman Riverway          North of Haywood Street           72.19%
 1000050     Wilma Dykeman Riverway          North of I-240                    72.19%
 1000064     Wilma Dykeman Riverway          North of Hill Street              52.84%
